are          being       fulfilled,     and        there         are        no       problems         or        deviations.
Emil: Starting from 2026, a new Water Code will be introduced in Kyrgyzstan, which provides for the possibility of selling
water to neighboring countries — both drinking water and irrigation water. In Soviet times such issues did not arise,
and all states emphasize in their constitutions that water must be treated with care. How does this relate to the current
situation?
Rysbekov Altynbek Durusbekovich: In essence, this question is a continuation of the previous one. All the states of the
region — Kyrgyzstan, Uzbekistan, Kazakhstan and Tajikistan — understand well how the system of water and energy
resources functioned in the Soviet period. At that time, natural resources, including water, gas and oil, were regarded
as common, and the republics supplied each other with the necessary volumes within a single system. After gaining
independence, each country fixed in its Constitution the list of natural resources located on its territory and considered
state property. Accordingly, water resources that form on the territory of Kyrgyzstan are legally a resource of the Kyrgyz
Republic, just as natural gas is a resource of the Republic of Uzbekistan, and similar resources are the property of
Kazakhstan. These are direct constitutional norms, the same for all states in the region. Nevertheless, despite the formal
differences in national legislation, the actual water supply to neighboring countries remains stable. Kazakhstan and
Uzbekistan today receive water in the same volumes that fully meet their needs, and there are no violations or
deviations on the part of Kyrgyzstan. Existing arrangements are being fulfilled, and there are no problems in this respect.
Emil: It is important to emphasize that the states of the region traditionally support each other, and water issues are
always resolved in a spirit of good neighborliness. Even if national legislation is developing, the principle of providing
water to neighboring countries remains unchanged. In this sense, no problems are expected.
Rysbekov Altynbek Durusbekovich: An intergovernmental agreement is now being developed that will regulate issues
of HPP operation and the allocation of water resources. It has already been noted that water is by nature a
transboundary resource, and Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan are conducting joint coordination on water and
energy issues.
Delegation of the Republic of Uzbekistan: The feasibility study also provides for an important point: in the vegetation
period, the operating regime of the Naryn HPP cascade will be revised. This will make it possible to increase the volume
of water supplied to downstream countries by more than 1.2 billion m³. For the countries located downstream, this is a
significant positive effect.

conditions.

Next question. Hello. What evidence do you have that the species pike-asp can successfully survive in the conditions of
large hydropower plants with reservoirs? Please name large reservoirs where stable populations of this species have

Deepti: I will answer. As for the evidence, most of the data on the species comes from the IUCN Red List assessment.
There are very few publications on this species. In the “Habitat and Ecology” section it is stated that the species is able
to survive in different types of water bodies, including reservoirs. This means that in the opinion of the author of the
assessment, Dr. Bakhtiyor Karimov, who published it in 2020, the species can exist under reservoir conditions. However,
if you ask whether we can name large hydropower reservoirs where stable populations have been observed precisely

significant numbers of this species were recorded in the Vakhsh River in Tajikistan. In the Amu Darya basin, the species
has always been more common than in the Syr Darya basin, where it is rare. And I once again draw your attention to
the          IUCN          assessment,          where          this        is         described          in         detail.

developed, and in coordination with local communities it will be determined what forms of visualization they need and
how best to present them.

Next question from Anna Rychkova: how are potential damages to the local community documented and compensated?
It is indicated that four aiyl okmotu are located in the impact zone, and a significant volume of inundation is expected.
Kydyralieva Narina: The process of consultations with the population will be carried out through the feedback
mechanism provided for in the World Bank’s environmental and social plans. Appropriate procedures will be developed,
including the procedure for establishing the fact of impact, the procedure for calculating compensation and the form of
payments. As in all such projects, all compensation costs will be completely transparent. Every payment, every amount
will be strictly recorded in accounting documents. Upon completion of the project, all costs, their purposes and
justifications will be reflected in the reporting — down to details and individual amounts. This information will be open
and accessible. As for the provision of data on specific individuals who received compensation, this is possible only with
the written consent of these citizens, since we are talking about personal information. If such consents are available,
the data may be provided, including official reports in written form.
The next question is why specialists from Uzbekistan were not involved in the development of the K-1 project, given
that the most experienced personnel are located there.
Delegation of the Republic of Uzbekistan: The answer is as follows: the project is being implemented jointly by three
countries, and the Uzbek side directly participates in the development of all key documents — the feasibility study, the
ESIA, as well as the intergovernmental agreement. There is an interdepartmental commission at work, and Uzbekistan
actively participates in all discussions and approvals. It is emphasized that there is no closed information. Both during
the development of the project and during its implementation, specialists from the three countries will always be
involved. After the creation of the joint company that will build and operate the plant, the participation of Uzbek
specialists will be formalized in official agreements. The extensive experience of Uzbek designers gained during the
construction of other hydropower facilities is always taken into account. In this regard, the doors are completely open
and cooperation will continue.


Final question: is it possible to obtain the cost estimate and the presentation?
Answer: the question is non-specific — it is not clear whether it refers to ESIA costs or to the costs of the project itself.
The author of the question will be contacted additionally and details will be clarified. AFRY added that the presentations
shown today will be posted on the PMO website, and access to them will be open. The cost of environmental and social
management measures has already been published in Chapter 14 and in the 22 thematic subprograms. And the
estimated construction cost of the HPP within the feasibility study is reflected in AFRY’s reports.

Question to the delegations of Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan: why was Kambarata HPP-1 approved before final
agreements among all three countries were reached and before the relevant intergovernmental agreement was
concluded?
Delegation of the Kyrgyz Republic: the main conditions have already been agreed. A decision has been made that the
operation of the plant will be carried out by a joint company whose founders will be the three countries — Uzbekistan,
Kazakhstan and Kyrgyzstan. Therefore we will directly participate in the management of the plant’s operating regime.
We have no doubt that operation will be regulated on a friendly basis. As for the expected increase in water volumes
during the vegetation period, according to our calculations it is not 50%, as was mistakenly mentioned, but
approximately 1.2 billion m³ of additional flow, which will be ensured by adjusting the operating regime of the Naryn
HPP cascade. The figure “50%” is unknown to us; perhaps it is a misunderstanding. But the fundamental conditions have




 P509251-1cf198a7-34a9-44bd-a9ad-c4249a506373.docx                                   Official Use Only           Page 114 of 182
Kambarata-1 HPP



indeed been agreed. The intergovernmental agreement is now undergoing legal processing, and certain details are being
clarified. We are confident that it will be agreed without difficulty.
Comment from the Republic of Kazakhstan: it is still difficult to speak of “approval.” The process is at the discussion
stage. As Deputy Minister Anatoly Druzbekovich noted, the operating regime will be agreed by all parties. As for today’s
topic — environmental issues — the organization of consultations is at a high level, for which we express our gratitude.
From our side, there is no final approval yet: there will be additional comments and further work on our positions.
Rysbekov Altynbek Durusbekovich: colleagues from Uzbekistan and Kazakhstan have rightly noted that the three
countries always find joint solutions that suit everyone. We have no disagreements, since cooperation on the water and
energy regime has been well established even before this project. In addition, we have generally constructive relations,
and this project is part of broader cooperation. Consultations are held regularly: approximately every 2–3 months a
meeting of representatives of the relevant agencies is held — the ministries of energy and water resources of
Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan. At such meetings, all issues related to the Kambarata HPP-1 project are
considered in detail. Agreed solutions are always reached. The intergovernmental agreement has already been drafted
and is now being agreed in both partner countries. Joint discussions of the document are planned in the coming days.
Then similar discussions will be held in Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan and Uzbekistan. There are no contradictions or problems
in this area.

Next question from Aleksandr Kolotov: the presenter on the CIA (cumulative impact assessment) noted the theoretical
possibility of using Kambarata HPP-1 to improve flows in the lower reaches, but discussed the obviousness and
limitations of this approach.
Robert: there is no reason to believe that Kambarata HPP-1, despite the significant volume of its reservoir, will lead to
additional shifting of flows from summer to winter. Such a shift in the regime can be carried out even without Kambarata
HPP-1 — by means of the existing Toktogul HPP. It should also be noted that there is potential to increase water releases.
The first question concerns the types of dams.
Emil: We indeed presented only one option, but it should be noted that the consultant considered fifteen possible dam
types. Following the analysis, the option that has been presented today was recommended. This option was studied
most thoroughly and included in the feasibility study.
Next question: if the results of comprehensive investigations — seismological, seismotectonic and others — turn out to
be unfavorable, will other options for location or solutions be considered?
Emil: Yes, they will. If the results differ significantly from the initial assumptions, then first of all the initial data will be
reanalyzed, and then possible alternative locations of the structures will be reviewed. This already relates to the next
design stage. There was also a comment that the area of the dissipation (energy dissipation) basin seems too small. This
question has been sent to the consultant; it is likely that recalculation or clarification will be needed in the next version
of the documentation.

The last question from the public foundation “Nash Veck”: what is the rationale for holding consultations in Stanglube?
Are they held within the framework of a grant or a loan?
Emil: all today’s consultations are held in accordance with the requirements of international financial institutions. This
is a mandatory part of the impact assessment and public consultation process. All questions that were asked online
have been processed. If those present have additional questions for the delegations of Kazakhstan, Uzbekistan or
Tajikistan, please ask them.
Delegation of the Republic of Uzbekistan: We had similar discussions earlier at an event in Istanbul and encountered
similar questions. A great deal of attention was paid to the watershed and flows in the Syr Darya basin. In Uzbekistan
we had similar questions regarding the Amu Darya basin. We have always emphasized that we strictly adhere to the
1992 intergovernmental agreements on the distribution of water resources in Central Asia. We are supporters of their
observance and would like participants and experts to also understand this context. Our colleagues from Kyrgyzstan
confirm a similar position. As I said earlier, there are currently no problems with the fulfillment of obligations among
the four countries. The agreements are observed, and the project being implemented does not violate the water
balance. We do not see any risks concerning water volumes during construction or operation. I thank my colleagues for
the confirmation — it is important that our relations and arrangements are stable and mutually respectful.

Delegation of the Republic of Uzbekistan (Shestian Vyacheslav, Ministry of Ecology of the Republic of Uzbekistan).
Thank you for presenting the Kambarata HPP-1 project — the presentation was very informative and the approach
professional. In the cumulative impact assessment (CIA) report I noticed the abbreviation SEA. Do I understand correctly
that this refers to a Strategic Environmental Assessment? And was the possibility of carrying out a Strategic
Environmental Assessment at an early stage — in a transboundary context — considered? Or is different terminology
being used?



 P509251-1cf198a7-34a9-44bd-a9ad-c4249a506373.docx                                       Official Use Only           Page 115 of 182
Kambarata-1 HPP



Robert: I may not be able to say directly whether such a possibility was officially considered. I mentioned Strategic
Environmental Assessment in order to show the place of this instrument in the hierarchy of procedures. The project is
now at the feasibility study stage. At this stage, it is the ESIA — the Environmental and Social Impact Assessment — that
is being carried out, and an Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP) is being developed. This is the next step
after the ESIA. SEA refers to another level — the strategic level — and is applied not at the level of an individual facility.

Delegation of the Republic of Uzbekistan (Shestian Vyacheslav, Ministry of Ecology of the Republic of Uzbekistan). I
have one more question. At the end of the presentation, you noted the need to take into account impacts in a
transboundary context — that is, in the lower reaches of the Syr Darya River. After carrying out the relevant
consultations and updating the ESIA materials, will the environmental release of water for the downstream countries
— Uzbekistan, Kyrgyzstan and Tajikistan — be revised? And will the 22 management plans be revised taking into account
the transboundary impact?
Zirgham: I may not have fully caught the wording of the question in the translation, but in general there are two parts.
First: the 22 management plans relate to impacts within the Kyrgyz Republic, that is, to the direct environmental and
social consequences of the construction and operation of the facility. Second: your question, as far as I understand,
concerns transboundary impacts and whether they will be taken into account in the management plans. The ESIA
mechanism is structured in such a way that the impact assessment covers the territory of K-1 and those impacts that
occur within the borders of Kyrgyzstan and within the area of responsibility of the PMO. For transboundary aspects,
separate processes and further intergovernmental discussions are envisaged, which must be conducted by the three
countries.
Robert: According to the available information, the cascade with Kambarata-1 can be operated in such a way that no
change in the water regime for the downstream countries is required.

Rysbekov Altynbek Durusbekovich: I would also like to add a little. Today we are discussing the main block — the impact
on the environment. As for the regime, volumes and procedure for water releases, separate meetings will be held on
these issues. As I mentioned earlier, these meetings are held at the level of the ministers of the three countries —
energy and water resources. It is at that level that issues of water regime, volumes, seasonality and water obligations
are considered in detail. This block will be discussed separately; I mention this now simply for information. As for today’s
topic — environmental impacts — I believe that we have provided sufficiently comprehensive information. The
consultants have also provided clear and specific answers. I thank them for this. And I thank all participants for their
questions.

A-2-4           Local Consultations (Aral village, Toktogul district) on the results of the
                Ecological and Social Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-
                power Plant Project Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP
 Location                 Aral Village, Atai Ayil Aimak (including Kargalyk AA)
 Date                     6 October 2025
 Time                     11:00 am – 2:30 pm
 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                       Checked/Approved by              Zirgham Afridi

Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having completed the environmental and social
assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts,
and proposed mitigation measures with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible and transparent manner,
ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential environmental and social impacts—such as land
use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from residents and
representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA and associated Environmental and
Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and
implementation align with both national regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World
Bank’s Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and inclusion, allowing
community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings and impacts identified
in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social aspects, including potential impacts during
construction and operation, and the corresponding mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic
had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and English, along with a Kyrgyz language
version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance with national requirements and international standards,




 P509251-1cf198a7-34a9-44bd-a9ad-c4249a506373.docx                                         Official Use Only          Page 117 of 182
Kambarata-1 HPP



public notices and letters were distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to
inform them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts ahead of the
consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the sessions.

Local Consultations (Nikche-Sai village, Toktogul district) on the results of the Ecological and Social Study Technical
Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes

 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Nikche-Sai village, Imanalyievskii Ayil Aimak

 Date                     9 October 2025

 Time                     12:00 pm – 3:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                         Checked/Approved by       Zirgham Afridi, 12 Nov 2025


Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having completed the environmental and social
assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts,
and proposed mitigation measures with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible and transparent manner,
ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential environmental and social impacts—such as land
use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from residents and
representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA and associated Environmental and
Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and
implementation align with both national regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World
Bank’s Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and inclusion, allowing
community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings and impacts identified
in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social aspects, including potential impacts during
construction and operation, and the corresponding mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic
had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and English, along with a Kyrgyz language
version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance with national requirements and international standards,
public notices and letters were distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to
inform them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts ahead of the
consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the sessions.

A-2-5           Local Consultations (Sary-Kamysh village, Toktogul district) on the results
                of the Ecological and Social Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1
                Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Sary-Kamysh village, Sary-Kamysh Ayil Aimak

 Date                     7 October 2025

 Time                     12:30 pm – 3:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                   Checked/Appr     Zirgham Afridi, 11 Nov 2025
                                                                oved by


Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having completed the environmental and social
assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts,
and proposed mitigation measures with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible and transparent manner,
ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential environmental and social impacts—such as land
use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from residents and
representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA and associated Environmental and
Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and
implementation align with both national regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World
Bank’s Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and inclusion, allowing
community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings and impacts identified
in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social aspects, including potential impacts during
construction and operation, and the corresponding mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic
had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and English, along with a Kyrgyz language
version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance with national requirements and international standards,
public notices and letters were distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to
inform them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts ahead of the
consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the sessions.

had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and English, along with a Kyrgyz language
version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance with national requirements and international standards,
public notices and letters were distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to
inform them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts ahead of the
consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the sessions.

                                                                                                            minimize soil and rock disturbance, reduce evaporation, and limit

                                                                                                         features will help regulate humidity, evaporation, temperature,
                                                                                                         precipitation, flooding, and wind, restoring natural microclimatic

                                                                                                         prevent excessive flooding. A real-time meteorological monitoring

A-2-7           Local Consultations (Toluk village (2nd meeting), Toktogul district) on the
                results of the Ecological and Social Study Technical Assistance for
                Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Toluk village, Toluk Ayil Aimak (2nd meeting)

 Date                     10 October 2025

 Time                     11:00 am – 2:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                      Checked/Approved by      Zirgham Afridi, 18 Nov 2025


Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having completed the environmental and social
assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts,
and proposed mitigation measures with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible and transparent manner,
ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential environmental and social impacts—such as land
use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from residents and
representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA and associated Environmental and
Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and
implementation align with both national regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World
Bank’s Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and inclusion, allowing
community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings and impacts identified
in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social aspects, including potential impacts during
construction and operation, and the corresponding mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic
had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and English, along with a Kyrgyz language
version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance with national requirements and international standards,
public notices and letters were distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to
inform them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts ahead of the
consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the sessions.

Kambarata-1 HPP


 No.    Participant      Question/Issue              Response
                                                                                  Regarding the change of the microclimate,
                                                                                  following a thorough microclimate impact
                                                                                  assessment, we have integrated a range of
                                                                                  mitigation measures into the Environmental and
                                                                                  Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) to protect local
                                                                                  climatic conditions.
                                                                                  This location was chosen specifically because it is
                                                                                  least likely to disrupt the existing microclimate.
                                                                                  We will use targeted excavation methods and
                                                                                  phased construction to minimize soil and rock
                                                                                  disturbance, reduce evaporation, and limit
                                                                                  temperature fluctuations. During reservoir filling,
                                                                                  water levels will be carefully monitored to avoid
                                                                                  sudden changes in temperature and humidity. We
                                                                                  will also track evaporation rates and temperature
                                                                                  variations throughout the process.
                                                                                  We are committed to ongoing communication
                                                                                  with local communities. We will keep you
                                                                                  informed about any potential microclimate
                                                                                  changes and actively seek your feedback on
                                                                                  challenges you may experience.
                                                                                  To further reduce microclimate impacts, we will
                                                                                  establish vegetated buffers and marshes around
                                                                                  the reservoir and dam. These natural features will
                                                                                  help regulate humidity, evaporation, temperature,
                                                                                  precipitation, flooding, and wind, restoring natural
                                                                                  microclimatic functions. Floodplain areas near the
                                                                                  reservoir will be monitored to prevent excessive
                                                                                  flooding. A real-time meteorological monitoring
                                                                                  system will be implemented to allow us to adjust
                                                                                  water flow and release timing, preventing
                                                                                  significant negative impacts.
                                                                                  We will regularly consult with residents to gather
                                                                                  observations on microclimate changes and
                                                                                  welcome suggestions for additional mitigation
                                                                                  measures as needed.
